# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Informer Cache Event Handler Chain

## Your Task

Trace the event handler chain from API server watch events to informer cache updates in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files implementing the ListWatch, the DeltaFIFO queue, and the cache.Store handler dispatch that notifies registered event handlers.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kubernetes informer cache event handler chain from API server watch events to informer cache updates. 

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a comprehensive analysis of the event handler chain, including:

### **Key Components:**

1. **ListWatch** - Provides Watch() and List() interfaces to consume API server events
2. **Reflector** - Pulls events from ListWatch and feeds them into DeltaFIFO via Add/Update/Delete
3. **DeltaFIFO** - Queue that accumulates state changes as Delta objects and handles initial sync via Replace()
4. **Controller** - Orchestrates Reflector and continuously pops Deltas from the queue
5. **sharedIndexInformer** - Main handler that updates the local cache indexer and dispatches notifications
6. **sharedProcessor** - Distributes notifications to all registered event listeners
7. **processorListener** - Relays events to user-registered ResourceEventHandlers with buffering and async dispatch

### **Event Flow:**
API Server Watch → ListWatch → Reflector.handleAnyWatch() → DeltaFIFO.Add/Update/Delete → DeltaFIFO.Pop() → processDeltas() → sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete → sharedProcessor.distribute() → processorListener (pop/run goroutines) → User's ResourceEventHandler

The answer includes all relevant files, symbols, the complete handler chain, and a detailed narrative explaining how each component contributes to delivering events from the API server to user-registered event handlers with proper synchronization, buffering, and cache consistency guarantees.

All are\\n32: // optional.\\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\\n34: \\n35: \\t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\\n36: \\t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\\n37: \\t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\\n38: \\t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\\n39: \\tKeyFunction KeyFunc\\n40: \\n41: \\t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\\n42: \\t// this queue \\\"knows about\\\". It is used to decide which items are missing\\n43: \\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\\n44: \\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\\n45: \\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n46: \\n47: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\\n48: \\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\\n49: \\t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\\n50: \\t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\\n51: \\t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\\n52: \\t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\\n53: \\tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n54: \\n55: \\t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\\n56: \\t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\\n57: \\tTransformer TransformFunc\\n58: }\\n59: \\n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n91: //\\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\\n94: // question are called \\\"known objects\\\" and this set of objects\\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\\n96: // (each in a different way).\\n97: //\\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\\n100: // different versions of the same object.\\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\\n102: \\t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\\n103: \\tlock sync.RWMutex\\n104: \\tcond sync.Cond\\n105: \\n106: \\t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\\n107: \\t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\\n108: \\titems map[string]Deltas\\n109: \\n110: \\t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\\n111: \\t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\\n112: \\t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\\n113: \\tqueue []string\\n114: \\n115: \\t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\\n116: \\t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\\n117: \\tpopulated bool\\n118: \\t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\\n119: \\tinitialPopulationCount int\\n120: \\n121: \\t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\\n122: \\t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\\n123: \\tkeyFunc KeyFunc\\n124: \\n125: \\t// knownObjects list keys that are \\\"known\\\" --- affecting Delete(),\\n126: \\t// Replace(), and Resync()\\n127: \\tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\\n128: \\n129: \\t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\\n130: \\t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\\n131: \\tclosed bool\\n132: \\n133: \\t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\\n134: \\t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\\n135: \\temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\\n136: \\n137: \\t// Called with every object if non-nil.\\n138: \\ttransformer TransformFunc\\n139: }\\n140: \\n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\\n142: //\\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\\n145: //\\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\\n148: //\\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\\n153: //\\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\\n158: \\n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\\n160: type DeltaType string\\n161: \\n162: // Change type definition\\n163: const (\\n164: \\tAdded   DeltaType = \\\"Added\\\"\\n165: \\tUpdated DeltaType = \\\"Updated\\\"\\n166: \\tDeleted DeltaType = \\\"Deleted\\\"\\n167: \\t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\\n168: \\t// relist. We don't know if the replaced object has changed.\\n169: \\t//\\n170: \\t// NOTE: Previous versions of DeltaFIFO would use Sync for Replace events\\n171: \\t// as well. Hence, Replaced is only emitted when the option\\n172: \\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is true.\\n173: \\tReplaced DeltaType = \\\"Replaced\\\"\\n174: \\t// Sync is for synthetic events during a periodic resync.\\n175: \\tSync DeltaType = \\\"Sync\\\"\\n176: )\\n177: \\n178: // Delta is a member of Deltas (a list of Delta objects) which\\n179: // in its turn is the type stored by a DeltaFIFO. It tells you what\\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\\n181: //\\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\\n184: type Delta struct {\\n185: \\tType   DeltaType\\n186: \\tObject interface{}\\n187: }\\n188: \\n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\\n191: type Deltas []Delta\\n192: \\n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\\n194: //\\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\\n198: //\\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\\n201: // modifications.\\n202: //\\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\\n204: // \\\"known\\\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\\n205: // affects error retrying.\\n206: //\\n207: //\\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\\n208: //\\texternal known object source.\\n209: //\\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\\n210: //\\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\\n211: //\\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\\n212: //\\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\\n213: //\\n214: //\\tExample:\\n215: //\\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\\n216: //\\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\\n217: //\\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\\n218: //\\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. The only exceptions are GetStore() and\\n219: //\\tGetIndexer() methods, which expose ways to modify the underlying\\n220: //\\tstorage. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\\n221: //\\tand internal tests.\\n222: //\\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\\n224: //\\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). See https://issue.k8s.io/86015 for details.\\n229: //\\n230: // Use `NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{..., EmitDeltaTypeReplaced: true})`\\n231: // instead to receive a `Replaced` event depending on the type.\\n232: //\\n233: // Deprecated: Equivalent to NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{KeyFunction: keyFunc, KnownObjects: knownObjects})\\n234: func NewDeltaFIFO(keyFunc KeyFunc, knownObjects KeyListerGetter) *DeltaFIFO {\\n235: \\treturn NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions(DeltaFIFOOptions{\\n236: \\t\\tKeyFunction:  keyFunc,\\n237: \\t\\tKnownObjects: knownObjects,\\n238: \\t})\\n239: }\\n240: \\n241: // NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to\\n242: // items. One is that the\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n69: //\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n74: // resync events.\n75: //\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n78: // the Pop() method.\n79: //\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n86: //\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n91: //\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n94: // question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n96: // (each in a different way).\n97: //\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n100: // different versions of the same object.\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\n102: \t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n103: \tlock sync.RWMutex\n104: \tcond sync.Cond\n105: \n106: \t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\n107: \t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\n108: \titems map[string]Deltas\n109: \n110: \t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\n111: \t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\n112: \t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\n113: \tqueue []string\n114: \n115: \t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has been populated\n116: \t// or Delete/Add/Update/AddIfNotPresent was called first.\n117: \tpopulated bool\n118: \t// initialPopulationCount is the number of items inserted by the first call of Replace()\n119: \tinitialPopulationCount int\n120: \n121: \t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\n122: \t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\n123: \tkeyFunc KeyFunc\n124: \n125: \t// knownObjects list keys that are \"known\" --- affecting Delete(),\n126: \t// Replace(), and Resync()\n127: \tknownObjects KeyListerGetter\n128: \n129: \t// Used to indicate a queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\n130: \t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\n131: \tclosed bool\n132: \n133: \t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether to emit the Replaced or Sync\n134: \t// DeltaType when Replace() is called (to preserve backwards compat).\n135: \temitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n136: \n137: \t// Called with every object if non-nil.\n138: \ttransformer TransformFunc\n139: }\n140: \n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\n142: //\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\n145: //\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\n148: //\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\n153: //\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\n158: \n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\n160: type DeltaType string\n161: \n162: // Change type definition\n163: const (\n164: \tAdded   DeltaType = \"Added\"\n165: \tUpdated DeltaType = \"Updated\"\n166: \tDeleted DeltaType = \"Deleted\"\n167: \t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\n168: \t// relist. We don't know if the replaced object has changed.\n169: \t//\n170: \t// NOTE: Previous versions of DeltaFIFO would use Sync for Replace events\n171: \t// as well. Hence, Replaced is only emitted when the option\n172: \t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is true.\n173: \tReplaced DeltaType = \"Replaced\"\n174: \t// Sync is for synthetic events during a periodic resync.\n175: \tSync DeltaType = \"Sync\"\n176: )\n177: \n178: // Delta is a member of Deltas (a list of Delta objects) which\n179: // in its turn is the type stored by a DeltaFIFO. It tells you what\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\n181: //\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\n184: type Delta struct {\n185: \tType   DeltaType\n186: \tObject interface{}\n187: }\n188: \n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\n191: type Deltas []Delta\n192: \n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\n194: //\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\n198: //\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\n200: // Replace, and Resync.  It may be nil if you do not need those\n201: // modifications.\n202: //\n203: // TODO: consider merging keyLister with this object, tracking a list of\n204: // \"known\" keys when Pop() is called. Have to think about how that\n205: // affects error retrying.\n206: //\n207: //\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\n208: //\texternal known object source.\n209: //\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\n210: //\tmodifies knownObjects. In Pop(), process function is called under\n211: //\tlock, so it is safe to update data structures in it that need to be\n212: //\tin sync with the queue (e.g. knownObjects).\n213: //\n214: //\tExample:\n215: //\tIn case of sharedIndexInformer being a consumer\n216: //\t(https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/blob/0cdd940f/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go#L192),\n217: //\tthere is no race as knownObjects (s.indexer) is modified safely\n218: //\tunder DeltaFIFO's lock. The only exceptions are GetStore() and\n219: //\tGetIndexer() methods, which expose ways to modify the underlying\n220: //\tstorage. Currently these two methods are used for creating Lister\n221: //\tand internal tests.\n222: //\n223: // Also see the comment on DeltaFIFO.\n224: //\n225: // Warning: This constructs a DeltaFIFO that does not differentiate between\n226: // events caused by a call to Replace (e.g., from a relist, which may\n227: // contain object updates), and synthetic events caused by a periodic resync\n228: // (which just emit the existing object). An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n47: //\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n52: //\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n65: // selector.\n66: //\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\n73: //\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n75: // during `Run()`.\n76: //\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\n84: //\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n91: //\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n96: // into its constituent parts.\n97: //\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n101: //\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n127: //\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n131: // to something else, for example through a\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n133: //\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\n138: \t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n139: \t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n140: \t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n141: \t// different handlers.\n142: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n143: \t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n144: \t// seen every item in the initial list).\n145: \tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n146: \t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n147: \t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n148: \t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n149: \t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n150: \t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\n151: \t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\n152: \t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\n153: \t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\n154: \t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\n155: \t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\n156: \t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\n157: \t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\n158: \t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\n159: \t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\n160: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\n161: \t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\n162: \tAddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n163: \t// RemoveEventHandler removes a formerly added event handler given by\n164: \t// its registration handle.\n165: \t// This function is guaranteed to be idempotent, and thread-safe.\n166: \tRemoveEventHandler(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error\n167: \t// GetStore returns the informer's local cache as a Store.\n168: \tGetStore() Store\n169: \t// GetController is deprecated, it does nothing useful\n170: \tGetController() Controller\n171: \t// Run starts and runs the shared informer, returning after it stops.\n172: \t// The informer will be stopped when stopCh is closed.\n173: \tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n174: \t// HasSynced returns true if the shared informer's store has been\n175: \t// informed by at least one full LIST of the authoritative state\n176: \t// of the informer's object collection. The PopProcessFunc\n569: // may return an instance of ErrRequeue with a nested error to indicate the current\n570: // item should be requeued (equivalent to calling AddIfNotPresent under the lock).\n571: // process should avoid expensive I/O operation so that other queue operations, i.e.\n572: // Add() and Get(), won't be blocked for too long.\n573: //\n574: // Pop returns a 'Deltas', which has a complete list of all the things\n575: // that happened to the object (deltas) while it was sitting in the queue.\n576: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Pop(process PopProcessFunc) (interface{}, error) {\n577: \tf.lock.Lock()\n578: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n579: \tfor {\n580: \t\tfor len(f.queue) == 0 {\n581: \t\t\t// When the queue is empty, invocation of Pop() is blocked until new item is enqueued.\n582: \t\t\t// When Close() is called, the f.closed is set and the condition is broadcasted.\n583: \t\t\t// Which causes this loop to continue and return from the Pop().\n584: \t\t\tif f.closed {\n585: \t\t\t\treturn nil, ErrFIFOClosed\n586: \t\t\t}\n587: \n588: \t\t\tf.cond.Wait()\n589: \t\t}\n590: \t\tisInInitialList := !f.hasSynced_locked()\n591: \t\tid := f.queue[0]\n592: \t\tf.queue = f.queue[1:]\n593: \t\tdepth := len(f.queue)\n594: \t\tif f.initialPopulationCount > 0 {\n595: \t\t\tf.initialPopulationCount--\n596: \t\t}\n597: \t\titem, ok := f.items[id]\n598: \t\tif !ok {\n599: \t\t\t// This should never happen\n600: \t\t\tklog.Errorf(\"Inconceivable! %q was in f.queue but not f.items; ignoring.\", id)\n601: \t\t\tcontinue\n602: \t\t}\n603: \t\tdelete(f.items, id)\n604: \t\t// Only log traces if the queue depth is greater than 10 and it takes more than\n605: \t\t// 100 milliseconds to process one item from the queue.\n606: \t\t// Queue depth never goes high because processing an item is locking the queue,\n607: \t\t// and new items can't be added until processing finish.\n608: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/103789\n609: \t\tif depth > 10 {\n610: \t\t\ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"DeltaFIFO Pop Process\",\n611: \t\t\t\tutiltrace.Field{Key: \"ID\", Value: id},\n612: \t\t\t\tutiltrace.Field{Key: \"Depth\", Value: depth},\n613: \t\t\t\tutiltrace.Field{Key: \"Reason\", Value: \"slow event handlers blocking the queue\"})\n614: \t\t\tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\terr := process(item, isInInitialList)\n617: \t\tif e, ok := err.(ErrRequeue); ok {\n618: \t\t\tf.addIfNotPresent(id, item)\n619: \t\t\terr = e.Err\n620: \t\t}\n621: \t\t// Don't need to copyDeltas here, because we're transferring\n622: \t\t// ownership to the caller.\n623: \t\treturn item, err\n624: \t}\n625: }\n626: \n627: // Replace atomically does two things: (1) it adds the given objects\n628: // using the Sync or Replace DeltaType and then (2) it does some deletions.\n629: // In particular: for every pre-existing key K that is not the key of\n630: // an object in `list` there is the effect of\n631: // `Delete(DeletedFinalStateUnknown{K, O})` where O is the latest known\n632: // object of K. The pre-existing keys are those in the union set of the keys in\n633: // `f.items` and `f.knownObjects` (if not nil). The last known object for key K is\n634: // the one present in the last delta in `f.items`. If there is no delta for K\n635: // in `f.items`, it is the object in `f.knownObjects`\n636: func (f *DeltaFIFO) Replace(list []interface{}, _ string) error {\n637: \tf.lock.Lock()\n638: \tdefer f.lock.Unlock()\n639: \tkeys := make(sets.String, len(list))\n640: \n641: \t// keep backwards compat for old clients\n642: \taction := Sync\n643: \tif f.emitDeltaTypeReplaced {\n644: \t\taction = Replaced\n645: \t}\n646: \n647: \t// Add Sync/Replaced action for each new item.\n648: \tfor _, item := range list {\n649: \t\tkey, err := f.KeyOf(item)\n650: \t\tif err != nil {\n651: \t\t\treturn KeyError{item, err}\n652: \t\t}\n653: \t\tkeys.Insert(key)\n654: \t\tif err := f.queueActionInternalLocked(action, Replaced, item); \"path\": \"tools/cache/shared_informer.go\", \"symbol\": \"processorListener.run\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes informer cache event handler chain traces the flow of events from the API server watch stream through the client-go informer machinery to user-registered event handlers.\\n\\n**1. ListWatch Interface (tools/cache/listwatch.go):**\\nThe ListWatch struct implements the ListerWatcher interface with two core methods:\\n- Watch(): Establishes a watch stream with the API server that streams watch.Event objects\\n- List(): Performs an initial list of objects from the API server\\n\\n**2. Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go):**\\nThe Reflector watches a specified resource and reflects changes into a store. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Entry point that calls ListAndWatch() in a retry loop\\n- ListAndWatch(): Orchestrates initial list via Reflector.list() and then watch via watchWithResync()\\n- handleAnyWatch(): Processes individual watch events from w.ResultChan() by calling store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete() based on event.Type (watch.Added, watch.Modified, watch.Deleted)\\n\\n**3. DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go):**\\nA queue that stores Deltas (lists of Delta objects representing state changes). Key methods:\\n- Add(obj): Creates an Added delta and enqueues it\\n- Update(obj): Creates an Updated delta and enqueues it\\n- Delete(obj): Creates a Deleted delta and enqueues it\\n- Replace(list): Syncs initial list by creating Sync/Replaced deltas and detecting deletions\\n- Pop(process): Dequeues a Deltas object and calls the process function (in the same critical section)\\n\\nDeltaFIFO accumulates all changes to an object as a Deltas slice, allowing consumers to see the complete history of changes while the queue was processing.\\n\\n**4. Controller (tools/cache/controller.go):**\\nLow-level controller that orchestrates Reflector and DeltaFIFO. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Creates Reflector with the ListerWatcher and Queue, starts Reflector.Run() and processLoop()\\n- processLoop(): Continuously calls Queue.Pop() with the Process function\\n- The Process function extracts Deltas and calls processDeltas()\\n- processDeltas(handler, store, deltas): Iterates through each Delta and:\\n  - Updates the local store (indexer)\\n  - Calls handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList) for Added/Sync/Replaced deltas\\n  - Calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj) for Updated deltas on existing objects\\n  - Calls handler.OnDelete(obj) for Deleted deltas\\n\\n**5. SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nImplements SharedInformer interface and acts as the main event handler. Key components:\\n- sharedIndexInformer struct: Contains indexer (cache.Store) and sharedProcessor\\n- HandleDeltas(obj): Called by processDeltas via controller, receives Deltas from DeltaFIFO, calls processDeltas() which invokes OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n- OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(addNotification{newObj, isInInitialList}, false)\\n- OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(updateNotification{oldObj, newObj}, isSync)\\n- OnDelete(obj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(deleteNotification{oldObj}, false)\\n\\n**6. SharedProcessor (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nResponsible for dispatching notifications to all registered event listeners. Key methods:\\n- distribute(notification, sync): Iterates through all listeners (processorListener instances) and calls listener.add(notification)\\n- Each listener receives the notification asynchronously\\n\\n**7. ProcessorListener (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nRelays notifications from sharedProcessor to one ResourceEventHandler using two goroutines and channels. Key components:\\n- handler: The actual ResourceEventHandler registered by the user (implements OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete)\\n- addCh: Receives notifications from processor.distribute()\\n- nextCh: Buffers notifications for the run() goroutine\\n- pendingNotifications: Ring buffer for notifications not yet dispatched\\n\\nKey goroutines:\\n- pop(): Pumps notifications from addCh to nextCh using the ring buffer, handling backpressure when nextCh is not keeping up\\n- run(): Receives notifications from nextCh and dispatches them:\\n  - addNotification \u2192 calls handler.OnAdd(newObj, isInInitialList)\\n  - updateNotification \u2192 calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\\n  - deleteNotification \u2192 calls handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\\n\\n**Complete Event Flow:**\\n1. API Server streams watch events \u2192 ListWatch.Watch() receives events\\n2. Reflector.watch() calls handleAnyWatch() to consume events\\n3. handleAnyWatch() calls store.Add/Update/Delete() for each watch event (DeltaFIFO)\\n4. DeltaFIFO creates Delta objects and enqueues them\\n5. Controller.processLoop() pops Deltas from DeltaFIFO\\n6. processDeltas() processes each Delta and calls sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n7. sharedIndexInformer updates indexer (cache) and calls processor.distribute()\\n8. processor sends notifications to all processorListeners\\n9. processorListener.pop() buffers notifications, processorListener.run() dispatches them\\n10. Finally calls user's registered ResourceEventHandler methods (OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete)\\n\\nThis multi-stage pipeline with buffering, synchronization points, and handler isolation ensures that:\\n- Watch events are reliably processed\\n- The local cache is always consistent\\n- Event handlers run asynchronously and independently\\n- Multiple handlers can be registered without blocking each other\"\n}\n",

server watch stream through the client-go informer machinery to user-registered event handlers.\\n\\n**1. ListWatch Interface (tools/cache/listwatch.go):**\\nThe ListWatch struct implements the ListerWatcher interface with two core methods:\\n- Watch(): Establishes a watch stream with the API server that streams watch.Event objects\\n- List(): Performs an initial list of objects from the API server\\n\\n**2. Reflector (tools/cache/reflector.go):**\\nThe Reflector watches a specified resource and reflects changes into a store. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Entry point that calls ListAndWatch() in a retry loop\\n- ListAndWatch(): Orchestrates initial list via Reflector.list() and then watch via watchWithResync()\\n- handleAnyWatch(): Processes individual watch events from w.ResultChan() by calling store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete() based on event.Type (watch.Added, watch.Modified, watch.Deleted)\\n\\n**3. DeltaFIFO Queue (tools/cache/delta_fifo.go):**\\nA queue that stores Deltas (lists of Delta objects representing state changes). Key methods:\\n- Add(obj): Creates an Added delta and enqueues it\\n- Update(obj): Creates an Updated delta and enqueues it\\n- Delete(obj): Creates a Deleted delta and enqueues it\\n- Replace(list): Syncs initial list by creating Sync/Replaced deltas and detecting deletions\\n- Pop(process): Dequeues a Deltas object and calls the process function (in the same critical section)\\n\\nDeltaFIFO accumulates all changes to an object as a Deltas slice, allowing consumers to see the complete history of changes while the queue was processing.\\n\\n**4. Controller (tools/cache/controller.go):**\\nLow-level controller that orchestrates Reflector and DeltaFIFO. Key methods:\\n- Run(): Creates Reflector with the ListerWatcher and Queue, starts Reflector.Run() and processLoop()\\n- processLoop(): Continuously calls Queue.Pop() with the Process function\\n- The Process function extracts Deltas and calls processDeltas()\\n- processDeltas(handler, store, deltas): Iterates through each Delta and:\\n  - Updates the local store (indexer)\\n  - Calls handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList) for Added/Sync/Replaced deltas\\n  - Calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj) for Updated deltas on existing objects\\n  - Calls handler.OnDelete(obj) for Deleted deltas\\n\\n**5. SharedIndexInformer (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nImplements SharedInformer interface and acts as the main event handler. Key components:\\n- sharedIndexInformer struct: Contains indexer (cache.Store) and sharedProcessor\\n- HandleDeltas(obj): Called by processDeltas via controller, receives Deltas from DeltaFIFO, calls processDeltas() which invokes OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n- OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(addNotification{newObj, isInInitialList}, false)\\n- OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(updateNotification{oldObj, newObj}, isSync)\\n- OnDelete(obj): Updates indexer and calls processor.distribute(deleteNotification{oldObj}, false)\\n\\n**6. SharedProcessor (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nResponsible for dispatching notifications to all registered event listeners. Key methods:\\n- distribute(notification, sync): Iterates through all listeners (processorListener instances) and calls listener.add(notification)\\n- Each listener receives the notification asynchronously\\n\\n**7. ProcessorListener (tools/cache/shared_informer.go):**\\nRelays notifications from sharedProcessor to one ResourceEventHandler using two goroutines and channels. Key components:\\n- handler: The actual ResourceEventHandler registered by the user (implements OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete)\\n- addCh: Receives notifications from processor.distribute()\\n- nextCh: Buffers notifications for the run() goroutine\\n- pendingNotifications: Ring buffer for notifications not yet dispatched\\n\\nKey goroutines:\\n- pop(): Pumps notifications from addCh to nextCh using the ring buffer, handling backpressure when nextCh is not keeping up\\n- run(): Receives notifications from nextCh and dispatches them:\\n  - addNotification \u2192 calls handler.OnAdd(newObj, isInInitialList)\\n  - updateNotification \u2192 calls handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\\n  - deleteNotification \u2192 calls handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\\n\\n**Complete Event Flow:**\\n1. API Server streams watch events \u2192 ListWatch.Watch() receives events\\n2. Reflector.watch() calls handleAnyWatch() to consume events\\n3. handleAnyWatch() calls store.Add/Update/Delete() for each watch event (DeltaFIFO)\\n4. DeltaFIFO creates Delta objects and enqueues them\\n5. Controller.processLoop() pops Deltas from DeltaFIFO\\n6. processDeltas() processes each Delta and calls sharedIndexInformer.OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete\\n7. sharedIndexInformer updates indexer (cache) and calls processor.distribute()\\n8. processor sends notifications to all processorListeners\\n9. processorListener.pop() buffers notifications, processorListener.run() dispatches them\\n10. Finally calls user's registered ResourceEventHandler methods (OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete)\\n\\nThis multi-stage pipeline with buffering, synchronization points, and handler isolation ensures that:\\n- Watch events are reliably processed\\n- The local cache is always consistent\\n- Event handlers run asynchronously and independently\\n- Multiple handlers can be registered without blocking each other\"\n}\n",
